Seattle Mariners season">2000</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #dcdcdc">Front office</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Owner(s)</th><td>\n<p>Baseball Club of Seattle, LP, represented by CEO <a href="/wiki/John_W._Stanton" title="John W. Stanton">John Stanton</a><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> (90%)\n</p>\nNintendo of America (10%)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Manager</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Scott_Servais" title="Scott Servais">Scott Servais</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">General Manager</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Jerry_Dipoto" title="Jerry Dipoto">Jerry Dipoto</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">President of Baseball Operations</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Kevin_Mather" title="Kevin Mather">Kevin Mather</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Seattle Mariners</b> are an American <a href="/wiki/Professional_baseball" title="Professional baseball">professional baseball</a> team based in <a href="/wiki/Seattle,_Washington" class="mw-redirect" title="Seattle, Washington">Seattle, Washington</a>. The Mariners compete in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB) as a member club of the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> (AL) <a href="/wiki/American_League_West" title="American League West">West Division</a>. The team joined the American League as an <a href="/wiki/Expansion_team" title="Expansion team">expansion team</a> in <a href="/wiki/1977_Major_League_Baseball_expansion" title="1977 Major League Baseball expansion">1977</a>. Since July <a href="/wiki/1999_in_baseball" title="1999 in baseball">1999</a>, the Mariners\' home <a href="/wiki/Baseball_park" title="Baseball park">ballpark</a> has been <a href="/wiki/Safeco_Field" title="Safeco Field">Safeco Field</a>, located in the <a href="/wiki/SoDo,_Seattle" title="SoDo, Seattle">SoDo</a> neighborhood of Seattle.\n</p><p>The "Mariners" name originates from the prominence of <a href="/wiki/Seamanship" title="Seamanship">marine</a> culture in the city of Seattle. They are <a href="/wiki/List_of_baseball_nicknames" title="List of baseball nicknames">nicknamed</a> the <b>M\'s</b>, a title featured in their primary logo from 1987 to 1992. They adopted their current team colors \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Navy_blue" title="Navy blue">Navy blue</a>, northwest green (<a href="/wiki/Teal" title="Teal">teal</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Silver_(color)" title="Silver (color)">silver</a> \xe2\x80\x93 prior to the 1993 season, after having been <a href="/wiki/Royal_blue" title="Royal blue">royal blue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gold_(color)" title="Gold (color)">gold</a> since the team\'s inception.<sup id="cite_ref-MarinersLogosAndColors_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MarinersLogosAndColors-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Their <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_mascots" title="List of Major League Baseball mascots">mascot</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Mariner_Moose" title="Mariner Moose">Mariner Moose</a>.\n</p><p>The organization did not field a winning team until 1991, and any real success eluded them until <a href="/wiki/1995_in_baseball" title="1995 in baseball">1995</a> when they won their first division championship and defeated the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> in the <a href="/wiki/American_League_Division_Series" title="American League Division Series">ALDS</a>. The <a href="/wiki/The_Double_(Seattle_Mariners)" title="The Double (Seattle Mariners)">game-winning hit in Game 5</a>, in which <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Edgar Mart\xc3\xadnez">Edgar Mart\xc3\xadnez</a> drove home <a href="/wiki/Ken_Griffey_Jr." title="Ken Griffey Jr.">Ken Griffey Jr.</a> to win the game in the 11th inning, clinched a series win for the Mariners, served as a powerful impetus to preserve baseball in Seattle, and has since become an iconic moment in team history.\n</p><p>The Mariners won 116 games in <a href="/wiki/2001_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2001 Major League Baseball season">2001</a>, which set the American League record for most wins in a single season and tied the <a href="/wiki/1906_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="1906 Chicago Cubs season">1906 Chicago Cubs</a> for the Major League record for most wins in a single season.\n</p><p>Through the <a href="/wiki/2017_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2017 Major League Baseball season">2017</a> season, the franchise has finished with a losing record in <a href="/wiki/List_of_Seattle_Mariners_seasons" title="List of Seattle Mariners seasons">28 of 41 seasons</a>. The Mariners are one of seven Major League Baseball teams who have never won a <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Series_champions" title="List of World Series champions">World Series championship</a>, and one of two (along with the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a>) never to have played in a <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> With the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bills" title="Buffalo Bills">Buffalo Bills</a> ending their 17-year playoff drought on December 31, 2017, the Mariners now hold the longest playoff drought in all of the four major North American professional sports, having not qualified for the playoffs since 2001.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Buhner Buzz Cut Night</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Rally_Fries"><span class="tocnumber">6.4</span> <span class="toctext">Rally Fries</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#King&#39;s_Court"><span class="tocnumber">6.5</span> <span class="toctext">King\'s Court</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#The_Maple_Grove"><span class="tocnumber">6.6</span> <span class="toctext">The Maple Grove</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Current_roster_and_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Current roster and Baseball Hall of Fame</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Baseball_Hall_of_Famers"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Baseball Hall of Famers</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Ford_C._Frick_Award_recipients"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Ford C. Frick Award recipients</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#State_of_Washington_Sports_Hall_of_Fame"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">State of Washington Sports Hall of Fame</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Minor_league_affiliations"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Minor league affiliations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Radio_and_television"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Radio and television</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Franchise_records_and_award_winners"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Franchise records and award winners</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Season_records_2"><span class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">Season records</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Career_records"><span class="tocnumber">10.2</span> <span class="toctext">Career records</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Footnotes"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Footnotes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seattle_Mariners&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Seattle_Mariners" title="History of the Seattle Mariners">History of the Seattle Mariners</a></div>\n<p>The Mariners were created as a result of a lawsuit. In <a href="/wiki/1970_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1970 Major League Baseball season">1970</a>, in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Pilots" title="Seattle Pilots">Seattle Pilots</a>\' purchase and relocation to Milwaukee as the <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Brewers" title="Milwaukee Brewers">Milwaukee Brewers</a> by <a href="/wiki/Bud_Selig" title="Bud Selig">Bud Selig</a>, the city of <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, <a href="/wiki/King_County,_Washington" title="King County, Washington">King County</a>, and the state of <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a> (represented by then-state attorney general <a href="/wiki/Slade_Gorton" title="Slade Gorton">Slade Gorton</a>) sued the American League for breach of contract.<sup id="cite_ref-suit_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suit-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>  Confident that Major League Baseball would return to Seattle within a few years, King County built the multi-purpose Kingdome, which would become home to the National Football League\'s expansion <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Seahawks" title="Seattle Seahawks">Seattle Seahawks</a> in <a href="/wiki/1976_NFL_season" title="1976 NFL season">1976</a>. The name "Mariners" was chosen by club officials in August 1976 from over 600 names submitted by 15,000 entrants in a name-the-team contest.<sup id="cite_ref-mchsnm_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mchsnm-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ken_Griffey,_Jr._June_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Ken_Griffey%2C_Jr._June_2009.jpg/190px-Ken_Griffey%2C_Jr._June_2009.jpg" width="190" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Ken_Griffey%2C_Jr._June_2009.jpg/285px-Ken_Griffey%2C_Jr._June_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Ken_Griffey%2C_Jr._June_2009.jpg/380px-Ken_Griffey%2C_Jr._June_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2098" data-file-height="2685" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ken_Griffey,_Jr._June_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ken_Griffey_Jr." title="Ken Griffey Jr.">Ken Griffey Jr.</a> holds six single-season batting records and an individual career record for the Mariners franchise.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Mariners played their first game on April 6, <a href="/wiki/1977_in_baseball" title="1977 in baseball">1977</a>, to a sold-out crowd of 57,762 at the Kingdome, losing 7\xe2\x80\x930 to the <a href="/wiki/California_Angels" class="mw-redirect" title="California Angels">California Angels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-game1box_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-game1box-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The first home run in team history was hit on April 10, 1977, by designated hitter <a href="/wiki/Juan_Bernhardt" title="Juan Bernhardt">Juan Bernhardt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\nThat year, star pitcher <a href="/wiki/Diego_Segu%C3%AD" title="Diego Segu\xc3\xad">Diego Segu\xc3\xad</a>, in his last major league season, became the only player to play for both the Pilots and the Mariners. The Mariners finished with a 64\xe2\x80\x9398 record, echoing the record the 1969 Pilots once held. In 1979, Seattle hosted the <a href="/wiki/1979_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="1979 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">50th Major League Baseball All-Star Game</a>. After the 1981 season, the Mariners were sold to California businessman <a href="/wiki/George_Argyros" title="George Argyros">George Argyros</a>, who in turn sold the team to <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Smulyan" title="Jeff Smulyan">Jeff Smulyan</a> in 1989, and then to Nintendo of America in 1992.\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:154px;max-width:154px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Seattle_Mariners_logo_1977_to_1979.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Seattle_Mariners_logo_1977_to_1979.png/150px-Seattle_Mariners_logo_1977_to_1979.png" width="150" height="69" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Seattle_Mariners_logo_1977_to_1979.png/225px-Seattle_Mariners_logo_1977_to_1979.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Seattle_Mariners_logo_1977_to_1979.png/300px-Seattle_Mariners_logo_1977_to_1979.png 2x" data-file-width="1092" data-file-height="504" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Mariners logo, 1977\xe2\x80\x931979</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Seattle_Mariners_logo_1980_to_1986.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Seattle_Mariners_logo_1980_to_1986.png/150px-Seattle_Mariners_logo_1980_to_1986.png" width="150" height="135" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Seattle_Mariners_logo_1980_to_1986.png/225px-Seattle_Mariners_logo_1980_to_1986.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Seattle_Mariners_logo_1980_to_1986.png/300px-Seattle_Mariners_logo_1980_to_1986.png 2x" data-file-width="695" data-file-height="625" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Mariners logo, 1980\xe2\x80\x931986</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Seattle_Mariners_logo_1987_to_1992.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Seattle_Mariners_logo_1987_to_1992.png/150px-Seattle_Mariners_logo_1987_to_1992.png" width="150" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Seattle_Mariners_logo_1987_to_1992.png/225px-Seattle_Mariners_logo_1987_to_1992.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Seattle_Mariners_logo_1987_to_1992.png/300px-Seattle_Mariners_logo_1987_to_1992.png 2x" data-file-width="628" data-file-height="628" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Mariners logo, 1987\xe2\x80\x931992</div></div></div></div>\n<p>During the 1992\xe2\x80\x9393 offseason, the Mariners hired manager <a href="/wiki/Lou_Piniella" title="Lou Piniella">Lou Piniella</a>, who had led the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a> to victory in the <a href="/wiki/1990_World_Series" title="1990 World Series">1990 World Series</a>. Mariner fans embraced Piniella,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and he would helm the team from <a href="/wiki/1993_in_baseball" title="1993 in baseball">1993</a> through <a href="/wiki/2002_in_baseball" title="2002 in baseball">2002</a>, winning two American League <a href="/wiki/Manager_of_the_Year_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Manager of the Year Award">Manager of the Year Awards</a> along the way.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2001_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2001 Major League Baseball season">2001</a> Mariners club finished with a record of 116-46, leading all of Major League Baseball in winning percentage for the duration of the season and easily winning the American League West division championship. In doing so, the team broke the <a href="/wiki/1998_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1998 New York Yankees season">1998 Yankees</a> American League single-season record of 114 wins and matched the all-time MLB single-season record for wins set by the <a href="/wiki/1906_in_baseball" title="1906 in baseball">1906</a> <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a>. At the end of the season, <a href="/wiki/Ichiro_Suzuki" title="Ichiro Suzuki">Ichiro Suzuki</a> won the AL <a href="/wiki/MLB_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="MLB Most Valuable Player Award">MVP</a>, AL <a href="/wiki/MLB_Rookie_of_the_Year_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="MLB Rookie of the Year Award">Rookie of the Year</a>, and one of three outfield <a href="/wiki/Gold_Glove_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold Glove Award">Gold Glove Awards</a>, becoming the first player since the <a href="/wiki/1975_in_baseball" title="1975 in baseball">1975</a> <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Fred_Lynn" title="Fred Lynn">Fred Lynn</a> to win all three in the same season.\n</p><p>On October 22, <a href="/wiki/2008_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2008 Major League Baseball season">2008</a> the Mariners announced the hiring of <a href="/wiki/Jack_Zduriencik" title="Jack Zduriencik">Jack Zduriencik</a>, formerly <a href="/wiki/Scout_(sport)" title="Scout (sport)">scouting</a> director of the <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Brewers" title="Milwaukee Brewers">Milwaukee Brewers</a>, as their general manager.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Weeks later, on November 18, the team named <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland Athletics</a> bench coach <a href="/wiki/Don_Wakamatsu" title="Don Wakamatsu">Don Wakamatsu</a> as its new field manager.  Wakamatsu and Zduriencik hired an entirely new coaching staff for 2009, which included former World Series MVP <a href="/wiki/John_Wetteland" title="John Wetteland">John Wetteland</a> as bullpen coach. The off-season also saw a litany of roster moves, headlined by a 12-player, 3-team trade that included sending All-Star closer <a href="/wiki/J._J._Putz" title="J. J. Putz">J. J. Putz</a> to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a> and brought 5 players\xe2\x80\x94including prospect <a href="/wiki/Mike_Carp" title="Mike Carp">Mike Carp</a> and outfielder <a href="/wiki/Endy_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Endy Ch\xc3\xa1vez">Endy Ch\xc3\xa1vez</a> from New York and outfielder <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Guti%C3%A9rrez" title="Franklin Guti\xc3\xa9rrez">Franklin Guti\xc3\xa9rrez</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a>\xe2\x80\x94to Seattle. Many of the moves, like the free agent signing of <a href="/wiki/Mike_Sweeney" title="Mike Sweeney">Mike Sweeney</a>, were made in part with the hope of squelching the clubhouse infighting that plagued the Mariners in 2008. It also saw the return of Seattle favorite Griffey Jr. The 2009\xe2\x80\x9310 offseason was highlighted by the trade for 2008 American League <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Award</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Lee" title="Cliff Lee">Cliff Lee</a> from the Philadelphia Phillies, the signing of third baseman <a href="/wiki/Chone_Figgins" title="Chone Figgins">Chone Figgins</a> and the contract extension of star pitcher <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="F\xc3\xa9lix Hern\xc3\xa1ndez">"King" F\xc3\xa9lix Hern\xc3\xa1ndez</a>.\n</p><p>Griffey Jr. announced his retirement on June 2, 2010, after 22 MLB seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:King_Felix_is_ready_(4667946841).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/King_Felix_is_ready_%284667946841%29.jpg/220px-King_Felix_is_ready_%284667946841%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/King_Felix_is_ready_%284667946841%29.jpg/330px-King_Felix_is_ready_%284667946841%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/King_Felix_is_ready_%284667946841%29.jpg/440px-King_Felix_is_ready_%284667946841%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:King_Felix_is_ready_(4667946841).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="F\xc3\xa9lix Hern\xc3\xa1ndez">F\xc3\xa9lix Hern\xc3\xa1ndez</a> has made five <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="Major League Baseball All-Star Game">All-Star</a> appearances as a member of the Seattle Mariners.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Mariners fired field manager <a href="/wiki/Don_Wakamatsu" title="Don Wakamatsu">Don Wakamatsu</a> along with bench coach <a href="/wiki/Ty_Van_Burkleo" title="Ty Van Burkleo">Ty Van Burkleo</a>, pitching coach <a href="/wiki/Rick_Adair" title="Rick Adair">Rick Adair</a> and performance coach <a href="/wiki/Steve_Hecht" title="Steve Hecht">Steve Hecht</a> on August 9, 2010. <a href="/wiki/Daren_Brown" title="Daren Brown">Daren Brown</a>, the manager of the AAA affiliate Tacoma Rainiers, took over as interim field manager. <a href="/wiki/Roger_Hansen" title="Roger Hansen">Roger Hansen</a>, the former Minor League catching coordinator, was promoted to bench coach. <a href="/wiki/Carl_Willis" title="Carl Willis">Carl Willis</a>, the former Minor League pitching coordinator, was promoted to pitching coach.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Mariners hired former Cleveland Indians manager <a href="/wiki/Eric_Wedge" title="Eric Wedge">Eric Wedge</a> as their new manager on October 19, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Dave_Niehaus" title="Dave Niehaus">Dave Niehaus</a>, the Mariners\' play-by-play announcer since the team\'s inception, died of a <a href="/wiki/Heart_attack" class="mw-redirect" title="Heart attack">heart attack</a> on November 10, 2010, at the age of 75.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In memory of Niehaus, Seattle rapper <a href="/wiki/Macklemore" title="Macklemore">Macklemore</a> wrote a tribute song called "My Oh My" in December 2010. He performed the song at the Mariners\' <a href="/wiki/Opening_Day" title="Opening Day">Opening Day</a> game on April 8, <a href="/wiki/2011_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2011 Major League Baseball season">2011</a>.\n</p><p>On April 21, 2012, <a href="/wiki/Philip_Humber" title="Philip Humber">Philip Humber</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a> threw the <a href="/wiki/Philip_Humber%27s_perfect_game" title="Philip Humber&#39;s perfect game">third perfect game</a> in Chicago White Sox history against the Mariners at <a href="/wiki/Safeco_Field" title="Safeco Field">Safeco Field</a> in Seattle. It was the 21st <a href="/wiki/Perfect_game" title="Perfect game">perfect game</a> in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">MLB</a> history.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Mariners starting pitcher <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Millwood" title="Kevin Millwood">Kevin Millwood</a> and five other pitchers combined to throw the tenth combined no-hitter in MLB history and the first in team history on June 8, 2012. The last combined one occurred in 2003, when six <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a> no-hit the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> in New York. The six pitchers used in a no-hitter is a major league record. <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="F\xc3\xa9lix Hern\xc3\xa1ndez">F\xc3\xa9lix Hern\xc3\xa1ndez</a> pitched the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Hern%C3%A1ndez%27s_perfect_game" title="F\xc3\xa9lix Hern\xc3\xa1ndez&#39;s perfect game">first perfect game</a> in team history, shutting down the <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">Tampa Bay Rays</a> 1-0 at <a href="/wiki/Safeco_Field" title="Safeco Field">Safeco Field</a> on August 15, 2012. It was the 23rd perfect game in Major League Baseball history.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The Mariners became the first team in Major League Baseball to be involved in a perfect game two times in one season.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>General Manager (GM) <a href="/wiki/Jack_Zduriencik" title="Jack Zduriencik">Jack Zduriencik</a> was relieved of his position by the team on August 28, 2015. <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Dipoto" title="Jerry Dipoto">Jerry Dipoto</a>, who formerly served as GM of the Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim, was hired as the new GM of the Mariners one month later.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> On October 9, 2015, manager <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_McClendon" title="Lloyd McClendon">Lloyd McClendon</a> was fired, and the search for a new manager was begun.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Scott_Servais" title="Scott Servais">Scott Servais</a> was named the new Mariners\' manager on October 23, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nintendo_of_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Nintendo of America">Nintendo of America</a> issued a press release on April 27, 2016, stating it would sell most shares it held of Seattle Mariners ownership to First Avenue Entertainment <a href="/wiki/Limited_partnership" title="Limited partnership">limited partnership</a>. Nintendo retained a 10% ownership share of the team after the sale was completed in August 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uniforms">Uniforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seattle_Mariners&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Uniforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Mariners donned their current uniforms in <a href="/wiki/1993_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1993 Major League Baseball season">1993</a> (with a slight change to the color arrangement made in 2015<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>). White jerseys and pants are worn for most home games, while gray jerseys and pants are worn on the road. In 2011, the team brought back an alternate "Northwest Green" jersey that was previously part of the uniform set from 1994 to 1996 to be worn during Friday home games.<sup id="cite_ref-adam_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adam-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> A navy blue alternate jersey is worn for occasional road games; other variations of a navy jersey had been used as home alternates prior to the reintroduction of the Northwest Green jersey.\n</p><p>A navy blue cap that features a ball and compass "S" logo is paired with the home white, road gray, and navy blue jerseys. A variation of this cap with a Northwest Green brim is worn with the home alternate jersey.\n</p><p>In January 2015 the team announced a new alternate uniform to be worn for Sunday home games. This cream-colored "fauxback" uniform features the current logo and lettering style in a royal blue and gold color scheme, a throwback to the original team colors. Unlike the rest of the uniform set, the back of the jersey does not display the player name.<sup id="cite_ref-adam_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adam-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NewSundayAlternate_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewSundayAlternate-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The cap features the current cap logo in the throwback colors.<sup id="cite_ref-NewSundayAlternate_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewSundayAlternate-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Spring_training">Spring training</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seattle_Mariners&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Spring training">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Peoria_Sports_Complex" title="Peoria Sports Complex">Peoria Sports Complex</a> in <a href="/wiki/Peoria,_Arizona" title="Peoria, Arizona">Peoria, Arizona</a>, has been the Mariners\' home spring training facility since 1994. The complex is shared with the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> On March 25, 2013, in a 16-0 victory over the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a>, the Mariners broke the team record for total home runs during a spring training season with 52.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_records">Season records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seattle_Mariners&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Season records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><i>This is a partial list listing the past 20 completed regular seasons. Although the Mariners took a major step forward in the power department, hitting the second most home runs in the American League (188 trailing Baltimore\'s 212), hitting fundamentals, questionable defense and a shallow pitching rotation and bullpen held the team back.  On September 27, manager Eric Wedge announced that he would not return for the 2014 season.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_McClendon" title="Lloyd McClendon">Lloyd McClendon</a>.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/2014_Seattle_Mariners_season" title="2014 Seattle Mariners season">2014</a>\n</td>\n<td>87\xe2\x80\x9375\n</td>\n<td>.537\n</td>\n<td>3rd\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>The Mariners made a surprising playoff run in 2014, but in the end, they fell short on the final day of the season. F\xc3\xa9lix Hern\xc3\xa1ndez won the AL ERA title with a 2.14 ERA and Robinson Can\xc3\xb3 had a career year in his first season with Seattle.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/2015_Seattle_Mariners_season" title="2015 Seattle Mariners season">2015</a>\n</td>\n<td>76\xe2\x80\x9386\n</td>\n<td>.469\n</td>\n<td>4th\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>McClendon was fired after the season ended.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> On October 23, 2015 <a href="/wiki/Scott_Servais" title="Scott Servais">Scott Servais</a> was hired as the team\'s new manager.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/2016_Seattle_Mariners_season" title="2016 Seattle Mariners season">2016</a>\n</td>\n<td>86\xe2\x80\x9376\n</td>\n<td>.531\n</td>\n<td>2nd\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>The Mariners made another surprising playoff run in 2016, but they ultimately fell short of the playoffs once again. The trio of Robinson Can\xc3\xb3, Nelson Cruz, and Kyle Seager all had stellar seasons themselves, but it was not enough to make the playoffs.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/2017_Seattle_Mariners_season" title="2017 Seattle Mariners season">2017</a>\n</td>\n<td>78\xe2\x80\x9384\n</td>\n<td>.481\n</td>\n<td>tied-3rd\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Safeco_Field">Safeco Field</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seattle_Mariners&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Safeco Field">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Has been home to the Seattle Mariners since the first game vs. the San Diego Padres on July 15, 1999. There were 44,607 people in attendance<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> that night.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Seattle_Mariners_Hall_of_Fame">Seattle Mariners Hall of Fame</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seattle_Mariners&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Seattle Mariners Hall of Fame">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners_Hall_of_Fame" title="Seattle Mariners Hall of Fame">Seattle Mariners Hall of Fame</a></div>\n<p>Seattle Mariners former chairman and CEO John Ellis announced on June 14, 1997 the creation of a Mariners Hall of Fame. It is operated by the Seattle Mariners organization. It honors the players, staff and other individuals that greatly contributed to the history and success of the Mariners franchise. It is located at the Baseball Museum of the Pacific Northwest<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Safeco_Field" title="Safeco Field">Safeco Field</a>.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Key\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="row">Year\n</th>\n<td>Year inducted\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="background:#ffb;"><b>Bold</b>\n</th>\n<td>Member of the <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">Baseball Hall of Fame</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="background:#ffb;"><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><img alt="dagger" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/37/Dagger-14-plain.png" width="9" height="14" data-file-width="9" data-file-height="14" /></div>\n</th>\n<td>Member of the Baseball Hall of Fame as a Mariner\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="background:#cfc;"><b>Bold</b>\n</th>\n<td>Recipient of the Hall of Fame\'s <a href="/wiki/Ford_C._Frick_Award" title="Ford C. 1997</span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table style="float:left; text-align:center; width:100px; border:#aaa 1px solid;"><tbody><tr><td style="background:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/File:Griffey-24.jpg" class="image"><img alt="24" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Griffey-24.jpg/100px-Griffey-24.jpg" width="100" height="80" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Griffey-24.jpg/150px-Griffey-24.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Griffey-24.jpg/200px-Griffey-24.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="480" /></a></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Ken_Griffey_Jr." title="Ken Griffey Jr.">Ken<br />Griffey Jr.</a><br />OF<br /><span style="font-size:80%; white-space:normal">Retired <span style="white-space:nowrap">August 6, 2016</span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table style="float:left; text-align:center; width:100px; border:#aaa 1px solid;"><tbody><tr><td style="background:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/File:Martinez-11.jpg" class="image"><img alt="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Martinez-11.jpg/100px-Martinez-11.jpg" width="100" height="80" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Martinez-11.jpg/150px-Martinez-11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Martinez-11.jpg/200px-Martinez-11.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="480" /></a></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Edgar_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Edgar Mart\xc3\xadnez">Edgar<br />Mart\xc3\xadnez</a><br />DH, 3B, Coach<br /><span style="font-size:80%; white-space:normal">Retired <span style="white-space:nowrap">August 12, 2017</span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The Mariners plan to retire uniform numbers only very selectively and subject to substantially higher expectations than those applied to the Mariners\' Hall of Fame. To be eligible to have one\'s number retired, in addition to the criteria outlined for the Mariners\' Hall of Fame, the former Mariners should have either:<br />&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;a) been elected to the National Baseball Hall of Fame and been in a Mariner\'s uniform for at least five years, or <br />&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;b) come close to such election and have spent substantially his entire career with the Mariners. <br />Eligibility shall not commence until after the former player has been voted on once for the National Baseball Hall of Fame, which for all practical purposes means six years after retirement.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ken_Griffey_Jr." title="Ken Griffey Jr.">Ken Griffey Jr.</a>\'s number <b>24</b> was retired at the beginning of the 2016 season, with the retirement ceremony taking place on August 6, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Griffey had been elected to the Hall of Fame in January of that year.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Edgar_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Edgar Mart\xc3\xadnez">Edgar Mart\xc3\xadnez</a>\'s number <b>11</b> was retired during the 2017 season, with the retirement ceremony taking place on August 12, 2017.  Mart\xc3\xadnez played his entire major-league career in Seattle and first appeared on the Hall of Fame ballot in <a href="/wiki/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_balloting,_2010" title="Baseball Hall of Fame balloting, 2010">2010</a>. His best Hall of Fame voting count was in 2018, when he received 70.4% of the vote (75% is required for induction).<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Jersey number 11 was not issued to anyone else between Mart\xc3\xadnez\'s retirement as a player in 2004 until his return to the Mariners as hitting coach in 2015.\n</p><p>Currently, only one other player has definitively met the requirements to have his number retired: <a href="/wiki/Randy_Johnson" title="Randy Johnson">Randy Johnson</a>, who played 10 seasons with the Mariners (1989\xe2\x80\x931998) and was elected to the Hall of Fame in 2015.\n</p><p>Despite not officially retiring number <b>19</b>, the team has not reissued it since <a href="/wiki/Jay_Buhner" title="Jay Buhner">Jay Buhner</a> left the team in 2001. \n</p><p>Number <b>51</b>, worn by <a href="/wiki/Randy_Johnson" title="Randy Johnson">Randy Johnson</a>, was withheld from players from 1998 until 2001, when it was issued to <a href="/wiki/Ichiro_Suzuki" title="Ichiro Suzuki">Ichiro Suzuki</a> upon his request after wearing it for his entire career in Japan. It was presumably taken out of circulation again, following Ichiro\'s 2012 trade to the Yankees coupled with Johnson\'s 2015 election into the Baseball Hall of Fame. The number was once again worn by Ichiro after he returned to the team in 2018.  \n</p><p>Number <b>14</b> (<a href="/wiki/Lou_Piniella" title="Lou Piniella">Lou Piniella</a>) was not given to any uniformed personnel between Piniella\'s 2002 departure and 2015, but it was issued to third-base coach <a href="/wiki/Manny_Acta" title="Manny Acta">Manny Acta</a> for the 2016 season.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a>\'s number 42 was retired throughout Major League Baseball on April 15, 1997.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Uniform_number_(Major_League_Baseball)" title="Uniform number (Major League Baseball)">Uniform number</a> <b>00</b> is presumed off-limits, as it has been worn by the Mariner Moose since 1997 (outfielder <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Leonard" title="Jeffrey Leonard">Jeffrey Leonard</a> was the last player to wear 00 for the M\'s, in 1990). From 1990 to 1996, the Moose wore the last 2 digits of the year of the current season.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seattle_Mariners&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small><i>(February 2014)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Louie_Louie">Louie Louie</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seattle_Mariners&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Louie Louie">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As part of the seventh inning stretch, after the crowd is led in singing "<a href="/wiki/Take_Me_Out_To_The_Ball_Game" class="mw-redirect" title="Take Me Out To The Ball Game">Take Me Out To The Ball Game</a>" or "<a href="/wiki/God_Bless_America" title="God Bless America">God Bless America</a>" the public address system begins playing the <a href="/wiki/The_Kingsmen" title="The Kingsmen">Kingsmen\'s</a> version of "<a href="/wiki/Louie_Louie" title="Louie Louie">Louie Louie</a>". This commemorates a 1985 prank attempt to make "Louie Louie" the state song of <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydroplane_Races_and_Cap-and-Ball_Game">Hydroplane Races and Cap-and-Ball Game</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seattle_Mariners&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Hydroplane Races and Cap-and-Ball Game">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As part of the mid-inning entertainment during games, three animated hydroplanes race on the Safeco Field Jumbotron screen. Each boat is "sponsored" by a local business. Fans are encouraged to cheer the boats on. The hydroplane races are inspired by actual hydroplane races held annually during <a href="/wiki/Seafair" title="Seafair">Seafair</a>, Seattle\'s primary summer event.\n</p><p>Similarly, in a separate event, a baseball is hidden underneath one of three animated Mariners baseball caps and the fans are encouraged to shout out which cap they think the ball is under at the end of the caps\' "dance." Both events are strictly for fun and no prizes are awarded.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buhner_Buzz_Cut_Night">Buhner Buzz Cut Night</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seattle_Mariners&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Buhner Buzz Cut Night">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1994, the Mariners started a promotion called "Buhner Buzz Cut Night" Inspired by <a href="/wiki/Jay_Buhner" title="Jay Buhner">Jay Buhner</a>\'s shaved head; any fan who was willing to have their head shaved before the game\xe2\x80\x94or was already bald\xe2\x80\x94would receive a free ticket to the game and a T-shirt with a slogan such as "Bald is Buhnerful" or "Take Me Out To The Bald Game". Hair 10 inches or longer was collected for charity. The promotion continued until Buhner\'s retirement in 2001, with a year\'s hiatus in 2000, and is still remembered by fans today.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rally_Fries">Rally Fries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seattle_Mariners&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Rally Fries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rally_fries_sign.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Rally_fries_sign.jpg/250px-Rally_fries_sign.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Rally_fries_sign.jpg/375px-Rally_fries_sign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Rally_fries_sign.jpg/500px-Rally_fries_sign.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rally_fries_sign.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> fans holding a sign requesting rally fries.</div></div></div>\n<p>Rally Fries are a baseball <a href="/wiki/Tradition" title="Tradition">tradition</a> started by Mariners broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Mike_Blowers" title="Mike Blowers">Mike Blowers</a> in 2007. During a game against the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a>, a fan tried to catch a foul ball along the right-field line but in turn spilled his tray of <a href="/wiki/French_fries" title="French fries">french fries</a> along the track. While chatting on the air and seeing the mishap, Blowers\' partner, <a href="/wiki/Dave_Sims" title="Dave Sims">Dave Sims</a>, suggested that he should send a new tray of fries to the fan. Blowers agreed, and sent his intern to deliver a plate of fries to the man.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the Mariners\' next game, fans made signs and boards asking Blowers for fries as well. Coincidentally, every time the fries were delivered, the Mariners seem to score or rally from a deficit, and thus the "Rally Fries" were created. This became so popular with the fans that signs were even seen when the Mariners were the visiting team, although on August 1, 2009, Blowers established that he only gives out fries at home games.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Generally, Blowers will select a person or a group of people that appeals to him, whether it is through fans wearing elaborate costumes or waving funny signs and boards. The fries are usually delivered from <a href="/wiki/Ivar%27s" title="Ivar&#39;s">Ivar\'s</a>, a Seattle-based seafood restaurant with a location at <a href="/wiki/Safeco_Field" title="Safeco Field">Safeco Field</a>. The amount of fries given out varies with the size of the winning group of fans. The winners are generally selected around the 5th or 6th inning, although potential candidates are shown in almost every inning beforehand.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="King.27s_Court"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="King\'s_Court">King\'s Court</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seattle_Mariners&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: King&#039;s Court">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As the 2011 season progressed, the Mariners marketing staff came up with an idea to encourage the growing fanbase of star pitcher "King" <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="F\xc3\xa9lix Hern\xc3\xa1ndez">F\xc3\xa9lix Hern\xc3\xa1ndez</a>. Every Hernandez start at Safeco Field is now accompanied by the King\'s Court, a designated cheering section for fans to sing, chant, and cheer while donning yellow T-shirts and K cards that are supplied by the team.\n</p><p>The King\'s Court is both a personal rooting section for Hernandez and trend-setter for Safeco Field. The team encouraged fans to dress like Larry Bernandez, Hernandez\'s alter ego from a Mariners TV Commercial, or show up in wacky costumes, rewarding the best with a ceremonial turkey leg.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Supreme Court is a special occurrence when the King\'s Court is extended to the entirety of Safeco Field. The first Supreme Court was F\xc3\xa9lix\'s first home game following his <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Hern%C3%A1ndez%27s_perfect_game" title="F\xc3\xa9lix Hern\xc3\xa1ndez&#39;s perfect game">perfect game</a> in 2012. Since then it has occurred each year at F\xc3\xa9lix\'s first home game of each season.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Maple_Grove">The Maple Grove</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seattle_Mariners&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: The Maple Grove">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The ultimately disappointing 2017 season had a few bright spots, including the establishment of the Maple Grove, a variation of the King\xe2\x80\x99s Court which honors <a href="/wiki/James_Paxton_(baseball)" title="James Paxton (baseball)">James Paxton</a> rather than F\xc3\xa9lix Hern\xc3\xa1ndez. At home games where Paxton starts, a group of fans sit by a Maple Grove banner, typically in the left field bleachers. A potted maple tree is also present in their section, provided by the Mariners; the Grove dubbed the tree "Stick Rizzs", in honor of long-time Mariners broadcaster Rick Rizzs.\n</p><p>When Paxton got to two strikes on a batter, the Grove held up \xe2\x80\x9cEh\xe2\x80\x9d Cards, a tip of the cap to Paxton\xe2\x80\x99s home country of Canada and a nod to the "K" (for strikeout) cards held up in King\'s Court. Variant cards have also been produced for special occasions, such as when a planned Paxton start turned into a Hern\xc3\xa1ndez start (a King\'s Grove, with "K\'eh" cards to cheer for Hern\xc3\xa1ndez). Other examples include when celebrating Paxton reaching 300 strikeouts, or in tribute to broadcaster Angie Mentink ("A" cards, to show support after she had publicly disclosed her being diagnosed with breast cancer). \n</p><p>The Maple Grove differs from the King\xe2\x80\x99s Court in that it was created and organized by fans, while the Court was promoted by the Mariners marketing team. When asked, Paxton stated that fans creating the Maple Grove was really special to him and that he never imagined that something of the sort would ever be done for him.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>The Grove continued throughout the 2018 season as well.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_roster_and_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame">Current roster and Baseball Hall of Fame</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a Nacional">Distrito Nacional</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_and_television">Radio and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seattle_Mariners&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Radio and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners_Radio_Network" title="Seattle Mariners Radio Network">Seattle Mariners Radio Network</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Seattle_Mariners_broadcasters" title="List of Seattle Mariners broadcasters">List of Seattle Mariners broadcasters</a></div>\n<p>The Mariners\' flagship radio station is <a href="/wiki/KIRO_(AM)" title="KIRO (AM)">KIRO-AM</a> (710 ESPN Radio), which previously broadcast Mariners contests from 1985 to 2002.  Former flagship stations include <a href="/wiki/KOMO_(AM)" title="KOMO (AM)">KOMO-AM</a> (2003\xe2\x80\x932008), and <a href="/wiki/KVI_(AM)" class="mw-redirect" title="KVI (AM)">KVI-AM</a> 570 (1977\xe2\x80\x931984). Television rights are held by <a href="/wiki/Root_Sports_Northwest" title="Root Sports Northwest">Root Sports Northwest</a>. During the 2016 season, the Mariners averaged a 5.84 rating and 103,000 viewers on primetime TV broadcasts.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> In years past, Mariners games have also appeared in Seattle on over-the-air stations <a href="/wiki/KING-TV" title="KING-TV">KING-TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/KIRO-TV" title="KIRO-TV">KIRO-TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/KZJO" title="KZJO">KTZZ-TV</a> (now KZJO), and <a href="/wiki/KSTW" title="KSTW">KSTW</a>.  Selected Mariners games are also available on Canadian television, due to an agreement between Root Sports Northwest and <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Sportsnet_Pacific" class="mw-redirect" title="Rogers Sportsnet Pacific">Rogers Sportsnet Pacific</a>.\n</p><p>Since 2013, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Rizzs" title="Rick Rizzs">Rick Rizzs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Goldsmith" title="Aaron Goldsmith">Aaron Goldsmith</a> have called games on the radio. The television broadcasts are anchored by play-by-play announcer <a href="/wiki/Dave_Sims" title="Dave Sims">Dave Sims</a> and color commentator (and former Mariners player) <a href="/wiki/Mike_Blowers" title="Mike Blowers">Mike Blowers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Seattle radio personality <a href="/wiki/Matt_Pitman" title="Matt Pitman">Matt Pitman</a> hosts the post-game show on the Mariners\' radio network, along with clubhouse reporter <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Drayer" title="Shannon Drayer">Shannon Drayer</a>.  Spanish-language radio broadcast duties are handled by Alex Rivera on play-by-play and former second baseman <a href="/wiki/Julio_Cruz_(baseball)" title="Julio Cruz (baseball)">Julio Cruz</a> providing color commentary.\n</p><p>The Mariners\' broadcast team for 2010 featured <a href="/wiki/Dave_Niehaus" title="Dave Niehaus">Dave Niehaus</a> and Rizzs\xe2\x80\x94back for their 32nd and 23rd seasons with the club, respectively\xe2\x80\x94as well as <a href="/wiki/Dave_Sims" title="Dave Sims">Sims</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Blowers" title="Mike Blowers">Blowers</a>. For the first three innings of each game, Niehaus worked the television broadcast with Blowers while Rizzs and Sims handled radio duties; after the third inning, Niehaus and Sims traded places. Niehaus, who had broadcast for the Mariners since their inaugural season of <a href="/wiki/1977_Seattle_Mariners_season" title="1977 Seattle Mariners season">1977</a>, died on November 10, 2010.  For the 2011 season, Dave Niehaus\' duties in the broadcast booth were filled by a collection of former Mariners broadcasters such as <a href="/wiki/Ron_Fairly" title="Ron Fairly">Ron Fairly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ken_Levine_(TV_personality)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ken Levine (TV personality)">Ken Levine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ken_Wilson_(sportscaster)" title="Ken Wilson (sportscaster)">Ken Wilson</a>; and former Mariners\' players such as Dave Valle, Dan Wilson, Jay Buhner, and Dave Henderson.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tom_Hutyler" title="Tom Hutyler">Tom Hutyler</a> has been the Mariners\' public address announcer since 1987, first at the Kingdome, and presently at Safeco Field.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>  While KOMO 1000 AM was the Mariners\' flagship radio station, Hutyler occasionally hosted the post-game radio show.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Franchise_records_and_award_winners">Franchise records and award winners</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seattle_Mariners&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section:
